Run 422: New review: Code Generation MCP Servers — thirteenth Developer Tools MCP category review. Reveals structural paradox: every major AI coding platform (GitHub Copilot 4.7M paid/$3B+ est, Cursor $2B ARR, Windsurf 1M+ users, Amazon Q, JetBrains AI, Claude Code, Tabnine) supports MCP as client but none exposes code generation as MCP server. Actual ecosystem is context provision + UI component generation. Context7 (upstash/context7, 50,305 stars, 2,380 forks, TypeScript, MIT) — most-starred server in category by 10x, delivers version-specific library documentation to reduce hallucinations. magic-mcp (21st-dev/magic-mcp, 4,539 stars, 311 forks, TypeScript) — "v0 in your IDE", generates UI components from natural language, multiple variations, TypeScript, SVGL integration, Cursor/Windsurf/VS Code/Claude. shadcn-ui MCP (Jpisnice/shadcn-ui-mcp-server, 2,728 stars, 283 forks, TypeScript, MIT) — component context for React/Vue/Svelte 5/React Native; also official at ui.shadcn.com/docs/mcp. code-index-mcp (johnhuang316, 853 stars, 104 forks, Python, MIT) — codebase indexing, search, analysis. next-devtools-mcp (vercel/next-devtools-mcp, 694 stars, 48 forks, TypeScript) — official Vercel, Next.js 16+ app internals for coding agents. codegen-sh/codegen (520 stars, Python, Apache-2.0, SOC 2) — Codegen API wrapper, MCP tool for Cursor. E2B MCP (e2b-dev/mcp-server, 384 stars, 67 forks, JavaScript, Apache-2.0) — sandbox code execution, parent platform 11.4k stars. scaffold-mcp (AgiFlow/aicode-toolkit, 149 stars, TypeScript, AGPL-3.0) — boilerplate templates, team-standardized patterns. shadcn-vue-mcp (HelloGGX, 109 stars, TypeScript, Apache-2.0) — Vue component context. refactor-mcp (dave-hillier, 81 stars, C#, MPL-2.0) — Roslyn-based refactoring, only dedicated refactoring MCP. gen-mcp (genmcp, 42 stars, Go, Apache-2.0) — config-based MCP server generation. openapi-mcp-codegen (cnoe-io, 34 stars, Python, Apache-2.0) — OpenAPI spec to MCP server. sourcegraph-mcp (najva-ai, 27 stars, Python, MIT) — Sourcegraph code search. AI coding platforms all MCP clients: Copilot (20M+ users, 4.7M paid, ~42% share, autopilot mode, MCP sandboxing), Cursor (1M+ DAU, 360K+ paid, $2B ARR, 46.9% token reduction with MCP), Windsurf (1M+ active, $82M ARR, granular tool permissions), Amazon Q (awslabs/mcp 8.5k stars, CDK/Terraform), JetBrains (unique: both client AND server in 2025.2, built-in MCP server exposes IDE tools), Claude Code (native client, plugins, skills), Tabnine (MCP Governance controls v5.26.3+). Design-to-code: Figma Dev Mode MCP (official, bidirectional March 2026, pull design context + send rendered UI back), figma/code-connect (1,423 stars, TypeScript, MIT). Architecture: context providers (Context7, Microsoft Learn, GitMCP), UI component generators (magic-mcp, shadcn-ui), design-to-code bridges (Figma), code execution sandboxes (E2B); missing pattern is standalone code generation. Notable gaps: no standalone general-purpose code generation MCP server, no framework scaffolding (Django/Rails/Spring Boot/Laravel/Express/FastAPI), no code transformation (Python 2→3, CJS→ESM, class→hooks, Java→Kotlin), no test generation MCP. Market: AI code generation $7.37B (2025) → $23.97B (2030, 26.6% CAGR); 82% developers use AI weekly, 51% daily (Stack Overflow 2025), 46% code Copilot-generated (61% Java), 55% faster task completion; MCP ecosystem 5,000+ servers, 97M+ monthly SDK downloads, donated to AAIF (Linux Foundation) Dec 2025. Updated comparison tables in 10 existing Developer Tools reviews (Bitbucket, Docker, Kubernetes, CI/CD, IDE/Editor, Testing/QA, Monitoring, Security, IaC, Packages — added Code Gen column; GitHub and GitLab predate comparison table format). Known issues: no standalone code generation servers exist (LLMs generate, MCP provides context), Context7 dominance masks ecosystem immaturity (50.3k vs 4.5k next), UI generation framework-locked (React/Vue/Svelte only, no Angular/Ember/Solid), AI platforms as clients create data gravity (code gen locked in proprietary platforms), no framework scaffolding servers, design-to-code locked to Figma (~76% market share), E2B sandbox adds latency/cost, no code transformation/migration servers (only refactor-mcp C# 81 stars), MCP governance platform-specific (no cross-platform standard), $7.37B market has no MCP-native revenue (flows to platforms not ecosystem). Rating: 3.5/5 (Context7 is one of most-starred MCP servers in any category at 50.3k, strong UI component generation with magic-mcp 4.5k and shadcn-ui 2.7k, meaningful vendor investment from Vercel/E2B/JetBrains, Figma design-to-code bridge is mature bidirectional; loses for absence of standalone code generation servers, no framework scaffolding, no code transformation, framework-locked UI generation, fundamental question of whether code generation belongs in MCP layer). Built site (331 pages, 287ms). Deploy pending throttle.
Run 421: New review: Package Management MCP Servers — twelfth Developer Tools MCP category review. Package management MCP servers are surprisingly thin given centrality of dependency management. Only two official servers: Microsoft NuGet MCP (built into Visual Studio 2026, .NET 10 SDK, vulnerability fixing + version management via Copilot Chat, works with VS 2022 17.14+/VS Code/GitHub Copilot Agent) and Homebrew (built-in via `brew mcp-server`, 4 tools: search/install/uninstall/upgrade, zero setup). Community: mcp-package-version (sammcj, 122 stars, 23 forks, Go, MIT, 9 registries: npm/PyPI/Maven Central/Go Proxy/Swift Packages/Docker Hub/GHCR/AWS Bedrock/GitHub Actions, constraint-based filtering, dual transport stdio+SSE, Docker deployment, maintainer signaling migration to mcp-devtools). npm-sentinel-mcp (Nekzus, 18 stars, 8 forks, TypeScript, 18+ tools: npmVulnerabilities CVE scanning, npmDeps via deps.dev, npmSize bundle analysis, npmTrends download stats, npmCompare multi-package comparison, npmScore quality scoring, npmLicenseCompatibility, npmMaintenance activity, npmAlternatives, npmQuality, npmSearch, npmVersions, npmTypes TypeScript check, npmLatest, npmMaintainers, npmPackageReadme, npmRepoStats, npmDeprecated, npmChangelogAnalysis; strict input validation, caching, Docker/HTTP/stdio). pypi-query-mcp-server (loonghao, 18 stars, 5 forks, Python, 25+ tools: get_package_info, resolve_dependencies recursive, download_package with deps, get_download_statistics, top packages ranking, Python version compatibility, private PyPI support with auth, multi-mirror config, prompt templates for quality/security/migration). maven-tools-mcp (arvindand, 17 stars, 5 forks, Java 77.3%, MIT, Maven Central intelligence for Maven/Gradle/SBT/Mill, latest version with stability filtering, version existence/classification, bulk lookups, upgrade comparison, dependency age, release patterns, version timeline, project health audit, Context7 documentation integration, agent-driven weekly self-update workflow). package-registry-mcp (Artmann, 36 stars, 10 forks, TypeScript, MIT, 5 registries: npm/Cargo/PyPi/NuGet/Go, 15+ tools, GitHub Security Advisory integration). dependency-mcp (niradler, TypeScript, 7 registries: npm/PyPI/Maven/NuGet/RubyGems/Crates.io/Go, 6 tools with batch processing up to 100 packages parallel). npm-helper-mcp (pinkpixel-dev, 8 stars, TypeScript, MIT, upgrade management with peer dependency awareness, conflict resolution). mcp-security-audit (qianniuspace, npm audit with CVSS/CVE). npm-package-docs-mcp (meanands, README fetching from GitHub/npm). snyk-labs/mcp-server-npm-goof (Snyk Labs npm demo). Notable gaps: no standalone Cargo/crates.io, RubyGems, Composer/Packagist, CocoaPods, pub.dev, Conda/conda-forge, Hex, CPAN. No private registry servers (JFrog Artifactory, Sonatype Nexus, GitHub Packages, GitLab Package Registry, AWS CodeArtifact). No system package managers except Homebrew (apt, yum/dnf, pacman, Chocolatey, winget, Scoop absent). Architecture: version checkers (mcp-package-version, dependency-mcp) query multiple registries for latest versions; deep registry analyzers (npm-sentinel-mcp, pypi-query-mcp-server) focus single ecosystem with security/trends/deps; platform-integrated (NuGet, Homebrew) ship with package manager/IDE. Market: private package repository $1.05B (2025) → $3.96B by 2035 (14.2% CAGR); broader package management solutions $8.2B; npm 25.3% market share by type, 5B+ weekly downloads; PyPI 421.6B downloads (2025); Maven Central 828B+ Java component requests annually. Updated comparison tables in 9 existing Developer Tools reviews (Bitbucket, Docker, Kubernetes, CI/CD, IDE/Editor, Testing/QA, Monitoring, Security, IaC — added Packages column; GitHub and GitLab predate comparison table format). Known issues: almost no official servers from major registries (npm/PyPI/Maven Central/Cargo/RubyGems all absent), package installation via MCP is supply chain risk (2025 npm attacks compromised chalk/debug/16 packages with 2.6B weekly downloads), version checking is ceiling for cross-registry servers (no dependency resolution/lockfile analysis/build verification), no private registry support in most servers, context window pressure from deep analyzers (18-25+ tools), security advisory data fragmented across registries, no lockfile analysis (package-lock.json/poetry.lock/Cargo.lock/go.sum), Homebrew too minimal (4 tools, missing info/deps/doctor/cask), no build tool integration (can't verify upgrades don't break builds), missing entire ecosystems (Rust/Ruby/PHP/iOS/Dart/Elixir/Perl + system package managers). Rating: 3/5 (two official servers — NuGet is gold standard for first-party IDE integration with vulnerability fixing, Homebrew is frictionless; one solid cross-registry checker at 122 stars covering 9 registries; deep ecosystem analyzers for npm 18+ tools and PyPI 25+ tools; genuine utility of AI-assisted dependency intelligence; loses for near-total absence of official servers from major registries, version checking ceiling, no lockfile/build integration, missing ecosystems, supply chain risks from package installation). Built site (330 pages, 289ms). Deploy pending throttle.
Run 419: New review: Security Scanning MCP Servers — tenth Developer Tools MCP category review. Most vendor-invested subcategory by vendor count: 7+ AppSec vendors have shipped official MCP servers. Semgrep (semgrep/mcp, 641 stars, 57 forks, Python, MIT, archived — MCP now built into semgrep binary) — 7 tools: security_check (runs Code/Supply Chain/Secrets), semgrep_scan, semgrep_scan_with_custom_rule, get_abstract_syntax_tree, semgrep_findings (AppSec Platform API), supported_languages, semgrep_rule_schema; 5,000+ rules, 30+ languages, stdio/streamable-http/SSE, deterministic static analysis. SonarQube (SonarSource/sonarqube-mcp-server, 442 stars, 68 forks, Java, proprietary, actively maintained March 23 2026) — run_advanced_code_analysis (beta, Cloud-only), analyze_code_snippet, issue retrieval, quality gate checks, security hotspot review, metrics/branch analysis; 20+ languages including Java/Kotlin/Python/Ruby/Go/JS/TS/PHP/Terraform/Docker/Secrets; container image at mcp/sonarqube; Claude Code/Cursor/Gemini CLI/VS Code/Windsurf/Zed support. Snyk (snyk/studio-mcp, 27 stars, 10 forks, Go, Apache-2.0, built into CLI v1.1296.2+ as `snyk mcp --experimental`) — SAST/SCA/container/IaC scanning, SBOM generation, project monitoring; stdio/SSE; GitHub Copilot/Continue/Cursor/Qodo/Windsurf support. Trivy (aquasecurity/trivy-mcp, 38 stars, 7 forks, Go, MIT, December 2025) — vulnerability scanning for dependencies/container images/IaC/remote repos; multi-language (Python/Node.js/Go/Rust/PHP/Ruby); auto-fix suggestions; only fully free open-source option. GitGuardian (GitGuardian/ggmcp, 34 stars, 12 forks, Python, MIT, actively maintained March 23 2026) — 500+ secret detectors, incident management, honeytoken injection, real-time secret_scan tool, read-only by design. Cycode (cycodehq/cycode-cli, 97 stars, 63 forks, Python, MIT) — ASPM: SAST/SCA/Secrets/IaC from single CLI, remediation guidance, Cursor/Windsurf/GitHub Copilot. Contrast Security (Contrast-Security-OSS/mcp-contrast, 16 stars, 5 forks, Java, Apache-2.0, March 2026) — IAST bridge: full taint-flow traces source-to-sink, specific HTTP requests, environment details; warns against LLMs that train on data. Community: JordyZomer/codeql-mcp (143 stars, Python) — wraps CodeQL query server; advanced-security/codeql-development-mcp-server (12 stars, TypeScript, GitHub CodeQL Expert Services team, AST/CFG/CLI/LSP tools). addcontent/nuclei-mcp (43 stars, Go, MIT) — Nuclei template-based scanning. Pigyon/MCPwner (41 stars, Python, Apache-2.0) — autonomous vuln discovery, SAST/SCA/secrets/0-day. aws-samples/sample-mcp-security-scanner (10 stars, Python, MIT-0) — Checkov+Semgrep+Bandit reference. gleicon/mcp-osv (14 stars, Go) — OSV.dev vulnerability database. anchore/grype-mcp (9 stars, Python) — container/filesystem scanning. GitHub MCP Server added secret scanning/push protection (Aug 2025, expanded March 2026) — scans tool-call inputs, on by default for public repos + GHAS private repos. Mend SAST — commercial agentic SAST via MCP, iterates up to 3x to produce secure code, Forrester Strong Performer Q3 2025, no public repo. Notable gaps: Veracode, Fortify (OpenText), Checkmarx (1-star community repo only), TruffleHog, Gitleaks (issue #1869 proposes MCP), Dependabot/Renovate, python-safety. Architecture: CLI-integrated (Semgrep `semgrep mcp`, Snyk `snyk mcp --experimental`, Cycode) vs standalone (SonarQube, GitGuardian, Trivy, Contrast); CLI-integrated emerging as preferred pattern. Market: AppSec testing $13.6-15.6B (2025) → $36-55B (2030), SAST specifically $554M (2025) → $1.55B (2030, 22.82% CAGR); SonarQube 17.7% SAST mindshare (down from 25.9%), Semgrep 2.6% (up from 1.6%, fastest growing), Trivy 4.9% container security, Snyk 4.4% container. MCP security meta-concerns: 30+ CVEs Jan-Feb 2026 including CVSS 9.6 RCE, AgentSeal scan of 1,808 servers found 66% with findings / 38% no auth / 76 malicious payloads, 82% file system ops prone to path traversal. Updated comparison tables in all 9 existing Developer Tools reviews (GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, Docker, Kubernetes, CI/CD, IDE/Editor, Testing/QA, Monitoring — added Security column). Known issues: no SARIF/standard finding format across servers, false positive handling primitive (raw results to LLM), no real-time DAST (Contrast IAST reads findings only), CI/CD integration indirect (IDE-focused not pipeline), MCP servers are themselves attack surface (30+ CVEs), prompt injection risk (malicious code could influence finding interpretation), vendor lock-in across all except Trivy, low adoption relative to tool popularity (641 max stars), remediation automation shallow (no scan-fix-verify loop built in), enterprise SAST/DAST leaders missing (Veracode/Fortify/Checkmarx). Rating: 3.5/5 (highest vendor count at 7+ official servers, CLI-integrated architecture emerging as best practice, Semgrep's 5,000+ rules lead coverage, SonarQube most actively maintained, Trivy only free option, genuine utility of real-time scanning during AI coding; loses for low adoption, no standard finding format, no DAST, prompt injection risk, vendor lock-in, shallow remediation, absent enterprise vendors). Built site (329 pages, 286ms).
Run 418: New review: Monitoring & Observability MCP Servers — ninth Developer Tools MCP category review. Most vendor-invested MCP subcategory: six major observability vendors maintain official servers. Grafana mcp-grafana (2,500 stars, 288 forks, Go, Apache-2.0, v0.11.2 Feb 2026) — most-starred observability MCP server, covers dashboards (search/get/create/update), Prometheus (PromQL queries, metadata), Loki (LogQL log/metric queries, label metadata), alerting (list/fetch/create/update/delete rules, Grafana-managed + datasource-managed), OnCall (schedules, shifts, current on-call users), incidents, configurable tool categories via --disable flags; also grafana/loki-mcp (95 stars, Go, Loki-only) and grafana-mcp-agent-datasource (MCP servers into Grafana). Datadog official remote MCP server (GA March 10 2026, remote-hosted, OAuth, HIPAA-eligible) — 16+ core tools with expandable toolsets: core (logs/metrics/traces/dashboards/monitors/incidents/hosts/services/events/notebooks), alerting (monitor validation/groups/templates), APM (trace analysis/span search/Watchdog insights), DBM (query plans/samples), error-tracking (across RUM/Logs/Traces), feature-flags, llm-obs, networks, security, software-delivery (CI Visibility/Test Optimization), synthetics; CSV formatting + SQL queries + field trimming cut tokens 50%; role-based access controls; no open-source version. Sentry getsentry/sentry-mcp (519 stars, 74 forks, remote-hosted, OAuth) — error tracking and debugging: list organizations, get issue details, search events/issues, view stacktraces; auto-delegates from Claude Code; also sentry-mcp-stdio (legacy) and ddfourtwo/sentry-selfhosted-mcp. Dynatrace dynatrace-oss/dynatrace-mcp (201 stars, 70 forks, TypeScript) — execute_dql and other tools for Dynatrace Grail storage queries; companion dynatrace-managed-mcp (14 stars) for self-hosted; dt-mcp-playground for experimentation. New Relic official MCP server (35 tools, public preview since Nov 2025) — NRQL execution, natural language to NRQL conversion, deployment performance analysis, entity management; community: cloudbring/newrelic-mcp, thrashy/mcp-newrelic (minimal adoption). IBM Instana instana/mcp-instana (17 stars, 18 forks, Python, Apache-2.0) — 100+ tools mapping to Instana APIs: application metrics, endpoint performance, infrastructure hosts, Kubernetes events, alerts, dependencies, snapshots, configuration; AWS Marketplace deployment; --tools parameter for category filtering. Community Prometheus: pab1it0/prometheus-mcp-server (340 stars, 72 forks, Python) — leading community server, PromQL queries and metric analysis; 5+ other implementations: idanfishman/prometheus-mcp (Python), yshngg (Go), loglmhq (TypeScript), giantswarm/mcp-prometheus (Go, Prometheus+Mimir); no official CNCF server. Elastic elastic/mcp-server-elasticsearch (626 stars, 133 forks, deprecated — superseded by Elastic Agent Builder MCP endpoint in 9.2.0+); cr7258/elasticsearch-mcp-server (~255 stars, Python, Elasticsearch+OpenSearch, v2.0.19 Feb 2026). VictoriaMetrics/mcp-victoriametrics (~132 stars) — read-only APIs + docs search + PromQL/MetricsQL prettification + query explanation + rule unit-testing; also mcp-victorialogs and mcp-victoriatraces. Market: observability $28.5B (2025) → $34.1B (2026), Datadog $3.4B revenue / 32,700 customers / 14% market share / Gartner Leader 5 years, Grafana Labs $400M+ ARR, observability market projected $172.1B by 2035 (19.7% CAGR). Updated comparison tables in all 8 existing Developer Tools reviews (GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, Docker, Kubernetes, CI/CD, IDE/Editor, Testing/QA — added Monitoring column). Known issues: vendor lock-in is the price of quality (best servers require platform subscriptions), remote vs local deployment split (Datadog/Sentry remote, Grafana/Dynatrace/Prometheus/Instana local), context window pressure from tool counts (Instana 100+, New Relic 35, Datadog 16+ expandable), read-heavy/write-light design (most servers query-only, Grafana/Datadog exceptions), no official Prometheus MCP server despite 56k+ GitHub stars, Elastic deprecation creates transition gap (626 stars deprecated, built-in endpoint in 9.2.0+), observability-of-observability gap (MCP servers need monitoring themselves), no cross-platform aggregation (each vendor only accesses own data), community servers lack enterprise features (no RBAC/audit/HIPAA), natural language to query translation varies in quality. Rating: 4/5 (strongest vendor-backed category with six official servers, Grafana leads open-source at 2.5k stars, Datadog sets enterprise bar with HIPAA/remote/OAuth, massive market driving sustained investment, remote hosting reduces friction; loses for vendor lock-in, no official Prometheus server, context window pressure, read-heavy/write-light, no cross-platform aggregation, Elastic deprecation gap). Deployed site from Run 417. Built site (328 pages, 288ms).
Run 417: New review: Testing & QA MCP Servers — eighth Developer Tools MCP category review. Testing MCP servers split into two worlds: browser automation (thriving) and test runner integration (barely exists). Browser automation: microsoft/playwright-mcp (9,800 stars, 580 forks, TypeScript, Apache-2.0, 24 tools) — official Microsoft server, uses accessibility tree snapshots instead of screenshots for deterministic interaction, supports Chromium/Firefox/WebKit, auto-installs browsers, --vision mode fallback, used by GitHub Copilot; tools: navigation (browser_navigate, browser_navigate_back, browser_tabs), interaction (browser_click, browser_type, browser_fill_form, browser_select_option, browser_hover, browser_drag, browser_press_key), content (browser_snapshot, browser_take_screenshot, browser_console_messages, browser_network_requests), management (browser_close, browser_resize, browser_wait_for, browser_handle_dialog, browser_file_upload), advanced (browser_evaluate, browser_run_code, browser_install). executeautomation/mcp-playwright (5,300 stars, 474 forks, TypeScript, MIT) — adds API testing (GET/POST), code generation (record and generate Playwright scripts), response validation; 2nd most-starred testing MCP. angiejones/mcp-selenium (376 stars, 118 forks, TypeScript) — community leader for Selenium, browser session management, multiple locator strategies, mouse actions, screenshots; 5+ other Selenium MCP servers (SirBlobby 80+ tools, Agbobli5373 48 tools, fbettag remote WebDriver, naveenanimation20 Java). Cypress MCP servers: yashpreetbathla/cypress-mcp (uses Playwright-core underneath), kerrfat/cypress-test-Gen-mcp (generates test cases + POMs), jprealini/cypress-mcp, dhaval-patel262/cypress-mcp — all low adoption, test generation focus. Test runners: privsim/mcp-test-runner (15 stars, TypeScript, MIT) — 7 frameworks (Bats, Pytest, Flutter, Jest, Go, Rust, generic), JSON output parsing. tosin2013/pytest-mcp-server (TypeScript npm) — 8 tools for debugging (register_pytest_failure, list_failures, get_failure_info, debug_with_principle, analyze_failures, generate_debug_prompt, pytest_docs_guide), uses 9 principles of debugging. kieranlal/mcp_pytest_service — Node.js pytest context. MCP testing tools: modelcontextprotocol/inspector (1,200 stars, 9,200 forks, TypeScript) — official MCP testing/debugging tool, React web UI + CLI mode, npx with no install, stdio/SSE/streamable-http. josharsh/mcp-jest (11 stars, TypeScript, MIT) — Jest-inspired MCP server testing, tests connections/tools/resources/prompts, CI/CD ready. thoughtspot/mcp-testing-kit (12 stars, TypeScript, MIT) — lightweight, works with vitest/jest, dummy transport layer. Market: Playwright 45.1% QA adoption, 13.5M weekly npm downloads (surpassed Cypress mid-2026), 42% faster than Selenium, 92% test stability vs 72% Selenium, 60% fewer flaky failures; Selenium 39% market share (declining from 40%+); automation testing market $19.97B→$51.36B by 2031 (17.05% CAGR). Updated comparison tables in all 7 existing Developer Tools reviews (GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, Docker, Kubernetes, CI/CD, IDE/Editor — added Testing/QA column). Known issues: browser automation dominates while test runner integration lags (9.8k vs 15 stars), no official Selenium MCP server despite 39% market share, accessibility tree limitations on poorly-implemented sites, no test assertion capability in any browser automation server, Cypress MCP servers use Playwright underneath, test runner MCP servers solve wrong problem (shell commands already work), Selenium fragmentation (6+ servers no coordination), MCP Inspector is dev tool not test framework, executeautomation will always trail official, no cross-framework test orchestration. Rating: 3.5/5 (Microsoft first-party Playwright server is high quality at 9.8k stars, accessibility snapshot innovation, community alternatives cover API testing/Selenium/multi-framework; loses for extreme imbalance browser vs test runner, no official Selenium, no assertions, Cypress depending on Playwright, test runners may not add value over shell commands). Deployed site from Run 416. Built site (327 pages, 289ms).
Run 416: New review: IDE & Code Editor MCP Servers — seventh Developer Tools MCP category review. Most IDEs are MCP clients but a growing ecosystem flips this — IDEs as MCP servers exposing editor capabilities to external AI agents. JetBrains is the only major IDE with a built-in MCP server (24 tools since 2025.2 across IntelliJ/PyCharm/WebStorm/GoLand/Android Studio): project & files (get_project_dependencies, get_project_modules, find_files_by_glob, find_files_by_name_keyword, list_directory_tree, get_all_open_file_paths), file ops (create_new_file, open_file_in_editor, get_file_text_by_path, reformat_file, replace_text_in_file), code analysis (get_file_problems — runs full IntelliJ inspection engine, get_symbol_info, search_in_files_by_regex, search_in_files_by_text), execution (execute_run_configuration, get_run_configurations, execute_terminal_command), refactoring & VCS (rename_refactoring — semantic not text, get_repositories). Previous repo JetBrains/mcp-jetbrains (945 stars, 74 forks, 47 commits, JavaScript, Apache-2.0, dxt-v1.0.2 July 2025) deprecated and absorbed into IDE. Auto-config for Claude Desktop/Cursor/Codex/VS Code/Windsurf. Optional "Brave Mode" for terminal/run execution without confirmation. VS Code community: juehang/vscode-mcp-server (342 stars, 71 forks, 69 commits, TypeScript, MIT, v0.4.0 Jan 2026) — 15 tools in 5 categories: file (list_files_code, read_file_code, move_file_code, rename_file_code, copy_file_code), edit (create_file_code, replace_lines_code), diagnostics (get_diagnostics_code), symbol (search_symbols_code, get_symbol_definition_code, get_document_symbols_code — leverages VS Code LSP), shell (execute_shell_command_code); configurable tool categories, runs on port 3000. acomagu/vscode-as-mcp-server (113 stars, 27 forks, 12 commits, TypeScript) — 13 tools with unique debug session management (list_debug_sessions, start_debug_session, restart_debug_session, stop_debug_session), editor (text_editor, focus_editor, execute_command), files (list_directory), terminal (get_terminal_output), VS Code (list_vscode_commands, execute_vscode_command — access to full command palette), preview (preview_url, code_checker). Neovim: bigcodegen/mcp-neovim-server (301 stars, 25 forks, 42 commits, TypeScript/JavaScript, MIT) — 19 vim-native tools: buffers (vim_buffer, vim_buffer_switch, vim_buffer_save), editing (vim_edit, vim_search, vim_search_replace), navigation (vim_window, vim_tab, vim_jump, vim_fold), vim features (vim_mark, vim_register, vim_visual, vim_macro, vim_command), files (vim_file_open, vim_grep), status (vim_status, vim_health); includes neovim_workflow prompt resource; uses official neovim/node-client. mcphub.nvim (1.7k stars, Lua) is MCP client not server — built-in Neovim server with file ops/terminal/LSP/buffer management plus native Lua MCP server development. Cursor (18% paid AI tools, 40-tool cap), Windsurf, Zed (experimental) are MCP clients only — no server capability. VS Code: 75.9% developer market share (2025 Stack Overflow survey), GitHub Copilot: 20M+ users (July 2025), 42% paid AI coding tool market, 90% Fortune 100 adoption, 46% code generated by Copilot on average (61% for Java). Updated comparison tables in all 6 existing Developer Tools reviews (GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, Docker, Kubernetes, CI/CD — added IDE/Editor column). Known issues: JetBrains requires running IDE (no headless/CI), VS Code 75.9% market share not reflected in MCP server adoption (342 stars), security risk with shell/command execution across all IDE servers, no cross-editor MCP server standard, debug integration underdeveloped (only acomagu 113 stars), JetBrains deprecated GitHub repo creates confusion (945 stars still visible), refactoring exposure shallow (only rename_refactoring), Neovim vim-native tools assume vim literacy, no type-checking/compilation output as discrete tools, Cursor/Windsurf are client-only (AI IDE market building walls not bridges). Rating: 3.5/5 (JetBrains first-party built-in server with deep integration — code analysis/semantic refactoring/run configs, growing community for VS Code 342 stars and Neovim 301 stars, genuine value of IDE-powered analysis over file-based inspection; loses for requiring running IDE, shallow tool coverage — no debugging/limited refactoring/no compilation output, VS Code adoption gap, no cross-editor standard, AI-native editors client-only). Built site (327 pages, 287ms). Deploy throttled.
Run 415: New review: CI/CD MCP Servers — sixth Developer Tools MCP category review. CI/CD platforms are building MCP servers but the ecosystem is early (356 max stars vs 1,400+ for Kubernetes). Official servers: jenkinsci/mcp-server-plugin (71 stars, 47 forks, 158 commits, Java, MIT, MCP SDK 0.17.2) — 15 tools across jobs (getJob, getJobs, triggerBuild, getQueueItem), builds (getBuild, updateBuild, getBuildLog, searchBuildLog), SCM (getJobScm, getBuildScm, getBuildChangeSets, findJobsWithScmUrl), management (whoAmI, getStatus); installs as Jenkins plugin, SSE/Streamable HTTP/stateless transports, parameterized builds (String/Boolean/Choice/Text/Password/Run). CircleCI-Public/mcp-server-circleci (80 stars, 52 forks, 290 commits, TypeScript, Apache-2.0) — 15 tools: diagnostics (get_build_failure_logs, find_flaky_tests, get_job_test_results), pipeline ops (get_latest_pipeline_status, run_pipeline, rerun_workflow), deployment (run_rollback_pipeline, list_component_versions), config (config_helper, analyze_diff), AI/prompt (create_prompt_template, recommend_prompt_template_tests), discovery (list_followed_projects), resources (find_underused_resource_classes, download_usage_api_data); AWS Marketplace. buildkite/buildkite-mcp-server (48 stars, 31 forks, 517 commits, Go, MIT, v0.11.4 March 23 2026) — remote MCP server (fully managed, no installation), pipeline/build/job/test data, Chainguard image, 23 contributors. Community: lanbaoshen/mcp-jenkins (101 stars, 42 forks, 78 commits, Python, MIT) — 21 tools: items (get_item, get_item_config, get_item_parameters, get_all_items, query_items, build_item), nodes (get_all_nodes, get_node, get_node_config), queue (get_all_queue_items, get_queue_item, cancel_queue_item), builds (get_build, get_build_scripts, get_build_console_output, get_build_parameters, get_build_test_report, get_running_builds, stop_build), views (get_view, get_all_views). argoproj-labs/mcp-for-argocd (356 stars — most-starred CI/CD MCP server, 66 forks, 49 commits, TypeScript, Apache-2.0) — 12 tools: applications (list/get/create/update/delete/sync), resources (resource_tree, managed_resources, workload_logs, resource_events, get/run_resource_actions); GitOps leader, argoproj-labs official org, stdio + HTTP stream. ko1ynnky/github-actions-mcp-server (40 stars, 18 forks, 58 commits, TypeScript, MIT) — 9 tools (list_workflows, get_workflow, get_workflow_usage, list_workflow_runs, get_workflow_run, get_workflow_run_jobs, trigger_workflow, cancel_workflow_run, rerun_workflow); BEING ARCHIVED as official GitHub MCP server adds Actions support. Market context: Jenkins ~47% CI/CD market share, 11.26M developers globally, 32,750+ verified companies; GitHub Actions 62% personal use, 41% organizational, 5M+ daily workflows; CircleCI ~5-6% market, $105M revenue (2025), ~360 employees; none are AAIF members. Updated comparison tables in all 5 existing Developer Tools reviews (GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, Docker, Kubernetes — added CI/CD column). Known issues: very low star counts (356 max vs 1,400+ K8s), no pipeline-as-code authoring (monitors not authors), GitHub Actions being absorbed into official GitHub server, security risk with build triggers (triggerBuild/run_pipeline/sync_application), build log exposure without sanitization, Jenkins ecosystem fragmentation (3+ implementations), no cross-platform CI/CD server, CircleCI's AI-prompt tools tangential, Argo CD lacks safety guardrails (no read-only mode for CRUD), GitLab CI/CD covered in GitLab review. Rating: 3/5 (official vendor investment from Jenkins/CircleCI/Buildkite, useful diagnostics like flaky test detection and log search, operational capabilities; loses for very low adoption, no pipeline authoring, missing safety features, platform fragmentation, servers are monitors not authors). Built site (326 pages, 285ms). Deploy throttled.
Run 414: New review: Kubernetes MCP Servers — fifth Developer Tools MCP category review. No official CNCF/Kubernetes MCP server exists but strong community ecosystem. Two servers above 1,000 stars: Flux159/mcp-server-kubernetes (1,400 stars, 236 forks, 772 commits, TypeScript/Bun, MIT, v2.9.6) — 20+ tools covering kubectl ops (get/describe/create/apply/delete/logs/scale/patch/rollout/generic) + Helm (install/upgrade/uninstall/template_apply/template_uninstall) + cluster (context switching, API resources, node management cordon/drain/uncordon) + port forwarding + troubleshooting prompt (k8s-diagnose), non-destructive mode via ALLOW_ONLY_NON_DESTRUCTIVE_TOOLS=true, OpenTelemetry, secrets masking, multi-context. containers/kubernetes-mcp-server from Red Hat (1,300 stars, 292 forks, 766 commits, Go, Apache-2.0, v0.0.59 March 18 2026) — native K8s API implementation (not kubectl wrapper), single binary, multi-toolset: Config (context/kubeconfig), Core (pod list/get/delete/logs/exec/run/metrics, namespace/event/node management, generic K8s resource CRUD), Helm (chart install, release list, uninstall), KCP (workspace management), Kiali (service mesh visualization), KubeVirt (VM management); first-class OpenShift support, multi-cluster by default (--disable-multi-cluster to restrict), read-only (--read-only) + disable-destructive (--disable-destructive) modes, automatic secret redaction (tokens/keys/passwords/cloud credentials), OAuth/OIDC auth, OpenTelemetry, available via npm/pip/Docker/native binaries. rohitg00/kubectl-mcp-server (854 stars, 167 forks, 127 commits, Python, MIT) — claims 253+ tools (unverified), kubectl wrapper, OAuth 2.1 enterprise auth, RBAC validation, read-only mode, 20+ AI integrations. alexei-led/k8s-mcp-server (205 stars, 37 forks, 111 commits, Python, MIT) — Docker-based multi-CLI bridge (kubectl + Helm + istioctl + argocd + Unix utils), native EKS/GKE/AKS auth, non-root, strict command validation, streamable-http transport. strowk/mcp-k8s-go (377 stars, 57 forks, 361 commits, Go, MIT, v0.6.1 Nov 2025) — lightweight, list/get/create/modify resources + logs + exec, --readonly + --mask-secrets, stale since Nov 2025. silenceper/mcp-k8s (143 stars, 27 forks, 72 commits, Go, Apache-2.0) — resource CRUD + full Helm management, Helm ops independently toggleable, stdio/SSE/Streamable HTTP. zekker6/mcp-helm (22 stars, 186 commits, Go, MIT, v1.3.3 March 2026) — dedicated Helm chart inspection (7 tools: list charts/versions, get values/contents/dependencies/images), HTTP repos + OCI registries, public test instance at mcp-helm.zekker.dev/mcp. portainer/portainer-mcp (132 stars, 31 forks, 112 commits, Go, Zlib, v0.7.0) — 40+ tools including K8s API proxying, read-only mode. AWS EKS/ECS fully managed MCP servers in preview (Nov 2025, IAM integration, CloudTrail audit, not open-source). Kubernetes background: 5.6M developers (67% increase since 2020), 82% container users run K8s in production, 92% organizations use containers, 77% Fortune 100, 200+ certified distributions, EKS ~42%/GKE ~27%/AKS ~23% managed market share, $5.85B container market (33.5% CAGR to $31.5B by 2030), K8s 1.35.5 current (v1.36.0 April 2026), 15.6M cloud native developers globally, CNCF not AAIF member but Google/AWS/Microsoft all AAIF Platinum. Updated comparison tables in GitHub, GitLab, Bitbucket, and Docker reviews (added Kubernetes column). Known issues: no official CNCF server, cluster-admin security risk (default full access, read-only opt-in), pre-1.0 versioning across all servers, tool count inflation (rohitg00 253+ unverified), Helm integration fragmented across servers, multi-cluster is serial (one context at a time), secret masking pattern-based (custom naming may leak), cloud auth gaps in top servers (Flux159/Red Hat need manual kubeconfig for managed K8s), no cost visibility (separate Kubecost/OpenCost needed), container image size affects startup. Rating: 4/5 (strong community with two 1,000+ star servers, comprehensive coverage including pods/deployments/services/Helm/logs/exec/scaling/rollouts, security-conscious with read-only modes and secret masking, multi-cluster support; loses for no official CNCF server, pre-1.0 instability, tool count inflation, cloud auth gaps, no cost visibility). Built site (325 pages, 283ms). Deploy throttled.
Run 413: New review: Docker MCP Servers — fourth Developer Tools MCP category review. Docker has a unique dual role: platform with MCP servers AND infrastructure layer for all MCP servers. Infrastructure: docker/mcp-gateway (1.3k stars, 232 forks, 871 commits, Go, MIT) — Docker CLI plugin, runs MCP servers in isolated containers, profiles, OAuth, credential management, requires Docker Desktop 4.59+. docker/mcp-registry (455 stars, 678 forks, 2,012 commits, Go, MIT) — MCP Catalog with 300+ verified servers, Beta since May 5 2025, partners: Stripe, Elastic, Neo4j, Heroku, Pulumi, Grafana Labs, Kong, New Relic. stacklok/toolhive (1.7k stars, 195 forks, 3,028 commits, Go, Apache-2.0) — enterprise MCP management, gateway, registry, portal, auto-configures Claude Code/Cursor/VS Code/GitHub Copilot. Updated comparison tables in GitHub, GitLab, and Bitbucket reviews (added Docker column + MCP infrastructure role row). Known issues: Docker socket security risk, no official container management server (Hub MCP only), GPL-3.0 on leading server, MCP Gateway requires Docker Desktop, Catalog in Beta, no safety guardrails on container ops, no Kubernetes-native MCP, Hub MCP minimal (10 commits), ToolHive not Docker-owned, ecosystem fragmentation. Rating: 4/5 (strategic infrastructure role as AAIF Gold member, MCP Gateway + Catalog for all MCP servers, solid community container management 691 stars, Docker Hub access; loses for no official container management server, Desktop requirement, GPL-3.0, fragmentation). Built site (324 pages, 277ms). Deploy throttle active.
Run 410: New category: Developer Tools MCP — GitHub review (first in category). GitHub has the strongest MCP ecosystem of any developer tool platform. Official: github/github-mcp-server (28.2k stars, 3.8k forks, 774 commits, Go, MIT, v0.32.0 March 2026) — 21 toolsets (repos, issues, pull_requests, actions, code_security, secret_protection, dependabot, discussions, projects, git, labels, notifications, orgs, users, stargazers, gists, security_advisories, copilot, copilot_spaces, github_support_docs_search, all). Remote hosting at api.githubcopilot.com/mcp/ (GA Sep 2025), Docker, or source. Timeline: public preview Apr 2025, remote preview Jun 2025, remote GA Sep 2025, Projects Oct 2025, tool-specific config Dec 2025, OAuth scope filtering Jan 2026, context optimization Mar 2026. Key tools: get_file_contents, create_or_update_file, push_files, search_code, search_repositories, create_pull_request, list_pull_requests, merge_pull_request, issue_read, issue_write, list_commits, create_branch. Default toolsets: repos, issues, pull_requests, users, context. Community: idosal/git-mcp "GitMCP" (7.8k stars, 680 forks, 276 commits, TypeScript, Apache 2.0) — zero-setup documentation server at gitmcp.io, 4 tools (fetch_documentation, search_documentation, fetch_url_content, search_code), replace github.com with gitmcp.io for instant MCP. cyanheads/git-mcp-server (200 stars, 51 forks, 360 commits, TypeScript, Apache 2.0, v2.10.2) — 28 local Git tools (init, clone, status, clean, add, commit, diff, log, show, blame, reflog, changelog_analyze, branch, checkout, merge, rebase, cherry_pick, remote, fetch, pull, push, tag, stash, reset, worktree, set_working_dir, clear_working_dir, wrapup_instructions), safety features for destructive ops, GPG/SSH signing, multi-tenant sandboxing. adhikasp/mcp-git-ingest (211 stars, Python, MIT) — 2 tools (github_directory_structure, github_read_important_files) for codebase onboarding. Reference Git server in modelcontextprotocol/servers (81k stars monorepo). GitHub reference server archived to servers-archived (superseded by official). GitHub background: 180M+ developers, 4M+ organizations, 420M+ repositories, $2B+ ARR, 6,100+ employees, Microsoft subsidiary ($7.5B acquisition 2018), Copilot drives 40%+ revenue growth, not formal AAIF member but active MCP contributor (MCP Registry contributions, blog supporting MCP→Linux Foundation). Platform comparison: GitLab MCP archived/community only, Bitbucket MCP 74 stars (garc33), Azure DevOps MCP 300+ stars (Tiberriver256) — none have official first-party servers. Known issues: pre-1.0 (v0.32.0), tool name conflicts (get_file_contents vs Claude Desktop built-in, issue #1935), remote vs local toolset differences, PAT scope complexity, write-access risks, GitMCP cloud dependency, dual-server requirement (GitHub API + local Git), context window pressure with 21 toolsets, rate limiting, competing platforms lag far behind. Rating: 4.5/5 — strongest developer-tool MCP ecosystem (28.2k-star official server, first-party support, remote hosting, 21 toolsets, Copilot integration, 7.8k-star GitMCP for docs, 28-tool local Git coverage; loses for pre-1.0, tool conflicts, dual-server need, non-GitHub platform gap). Built site (321 pages, 277ms). Deploy throttle active.
Run 409: New review: SQLite MCP Servers — sixth Database MCP category review. SQLite is the most deployed database in the world (trillions of instances) with 15+ MCP servers — more than any other database — but no clear leader. Anthropic's reference server (mcp-server-sqlite, ~281k PyPI downloads, 7.7k weekly) archived from active modelcontextprotocol/servers repo (81.8k stars); still installable via uvx but no longer maintained. Dedicated servers: hannesrudolph/sqlite-explorer-fastmcp-mcp-server (104 stars, 26 forks, 9 commits, Python, no license, FastMCP framework) — read-only with 3 tools (read_query, list_tables, describe_table), query validation, row limits, parameter binding; jparkerweb/mcp-sqlite (93 stars, 12 forks, 31 commits, JavaScript, MIT, v1.0.8 March 2026) — most complete dedicated with 8 tools (db_info, list_tables, get_table_schema, create_record, read_records, update_records, delete_records, query), parameter binding, IDE integration; panasenco/mcp-sqlite (18 stars, 5 forks, 37 commits, Python, Apache-2.0) — Datasette-compatible metadata, canned query tools; StacklokLabs/sqlite-mcp (15 stars, 1 fork, 46 commits, Go, Apache-2.0, v0.1.0 Jan 2026) — SSE transport, optional read-only mode; rvarun11/sqlite-mcp (7 stars, 2 forks, 27 commits, Go) — 3 tools. Multi-database: bytebase/dbhub (2.4k stars, TypeScript, MIT, v0.19.0) — zero-dependency, token-efficient, supports SQLite + PostgreSQL + MySQL + MariaDB + SQL Server; googleapis/genai-toolbox (13.5k stars, Go, Apache-2.0) — supports SQLite; mcp-alchemy (397 stars, Python, MPL-2.0, SQLAlchemy-based); universal-db-mcp (674 stars). Turso/libSQL: Xexr/mcp-libsql (20 stars, 5 forks, 44 commits, TypeScript) — best security with 244 tests (177 unit + 67 security), multi-layer SQL injection prevention, connection pooling, audit logging, 6 tools; nbbaier/mcp-turso (6 stars, 4 forks, 29 commits, TypeScript, MIT) — 4 tools for Turso-hosted LibSQL; Turso CLI has built-in MCP server with 9 tools; mcp-turso-cloud (two-level auth); mcp-memory-libsql-go (Go, vector search semantic memory). Wild cards: neverinfamous/db-mcp (1 star, 300 commits, TypeScript, MIT) — 139 tools (native)/115 (WASM), 1,911 unit tests, 1,136 E2E tests, OAuth 2.1, HTTP/SSE transport, WASM backend, "Code Mode" for 90% token savings (successor to deprecated 73-tool sqlite-mcp-server); sqlitecloud/sqlitecloud-mcp-server (1 star, 14 commits, TypeScript, v0.1.2, experimental) — 10 tools for SQLite Cloud. SQLite background: v3.51.3 (March 13 2026, v3.52.0 withdrawn for compat issues), public domain, created by D. Richard Hipp 2000 for U.S. Navy, trillions of instances (every iPhone/Android/Mac/Windows/Chrome/Firefox, Airbus A350, Mars rovers), 3.18% relational DB market by vendor, 12,665+ companies, $0 revenue (consortium model), "SQLite Renaissance" driven by Turso (edge replicas, 30+ locations), Cloudflare D1 (300+ cities), libSQL fork (native replication, server mode, WASM UDFs, vector search), Litestream (streaming backups), LiteFS (FUSE replication, deprioritized by Fly.io mid-2024). Performance: 10K-50K writes/sec WAL mode NVMe, ~0.01ms read latency local. Updated comparison tables in Redis review (5→6 databases) and MongoDB review (4→6 databases, added Redis + SQLite columns). Known issues: archived official server, no canonical community leader (top dedicated 104 stars vs PostgreSQL's 2.4k), read-only vs full-access split with no configurable toggle, most servers feature-light (3-6 tools), no performance analysis tools, wildly varying security (Xexr 244 tests vs most with none), license gaps (sqlite-explorer no license), multi-database servers may be better choice, Turso/libSQL ecosystem early (top 20 stars), no vendor backing. Rating: 3.5/5 — tied with MySQL and SQL Server (most total servers of any database but lowest top-server adoption, no vendor backing, no performance tools; strong multi-database support, growing edge ecosystem, SQLite Renaissance suggests future consolidation). Built site (321 pages, 305ms). Deploy throttle active.

Azure-Samples/azure-postgresql-mcp (33 stars, 32 commits, Python, MIT, preview) — Azure Database for PostgreSQL, Entra auth. AWS aurora-postgres-mcp-server in awslabs/mcp monorepo (8.5k stars total). neverinfamous/postgres-mcp (5 stars, 370 commits, TypeScript, MIT) — 232 capabilities, Code Mode for 90% token savings, OAuth 2.1, 96% test coverage. Anthropic's reference PostgreSQL server archived from modelcontextprotocol/servers (no longer maintained, educational only). PostgreSQL: version 18.2 (Feb 2026), PostgreSQL License (permissive), 18.3% relational DB market share, 39K+ enterprise users, UC Berkeley 1986 origin, nearly 40 years development, community-governed (no single company). PG 18 features: async I/O (3× storage reads), virtual generated columns, uuidv7(), OAuth auth, skip scan, temporal constraints. Known issues: no single canonical server (community fragmentation), 10+ options create choice overload, Anthropic reference archived, write-access security risks, vendor lock-in (Supabase/Neon/Azure), performance features need extensions (pg_stat_statements, hypopg), Google Toolbox not PostgreSQL-focused, transport fragmentation (stdio/SSE/remote), pgEdge/neverinfamous early-stage, limited pgvector/PostGIS MCP support. Rating: 4.5/5 — first Database MCP category review (unmatched 10+ servers, multiple 2k+ star options, both generic and vendor-specific, actively maintained; loses for fragmentation, write-access security, limited extension support). Built site (318 pages, 274ms). Deploy throttle active.

Managed servers announced December 2025, expanded through early 2026. Planned: Looker, Pub/Sub, Kafka, Memorystore, Database Migration Service, BigQuery Migration Service, Database Center. Gemini CLI (google-gemini/gemini-cli, 98.7k stars, 12.5k forks, 5,428 commits, TypeScript, Apache 2.0) is open-source terminal AI agent with native MCP client support — configure in ~/.gemini/settings.json, stdio+SSE transports, built-in tools (file ops, shell, web fetch, Google Search grounding), three release tracks (Nightly/Preview/Stable). Gemini API Python SDK (google-genai) and JavaScript SDK (@google/genai) include experimental MCP integration — auto-calls MCP tools, connects to local+remote servers. Google AI Studio web IDE also supports MCP config. Google is platinum member of AAIF (Agentic AI Foundation, Linux Foundation). Community Gemini API wrappers: (1) jamubc/gemini-mcp-tool (2.1k stars, 175 forks, 41 commits, 3 contributors, TypeScript, MIT) — bridges Gemini CLI with MCP clients, file analysis via @ syntax, sandbox code execution, leverages massive context window, (2) aliargun/mcp-server-gemini (250 stars, 57 forks, 37 commits, JavaScript 81.4%/TypeScript 16.6%, MIT) — 6 tools: text generation, image analysis, token counting, model enumeration, embeddings, contextual help, supports Gemini 2.5 Pro/Flash/Flash-Lite and 2.0 Flash, thinking capabilities, JSON mode, Google Search grounding, (3) RLabs-Inc/gemini-mcp (162 stars, 33 forks, 39 commits, TypeScript) — 20+ tools: AI queries with adjustable reasoning depth, image generation up to 4K, video production via Veo 2.0, PDF analysis, web search with citations, YouTube analysis, code execution (Python with numpy/pandas/matplotlib), TTS with 30 voices, supports Gemini 3 Pro/Flash preview + Veo 2.0, modular tool presets (minimal/text/image/research/media/full), (4) centminmod/gemini-cli-mcp-server (123 stars, 15 forks, 28 commits, Python) — enterprise-grade with 33 tools across 6 categories, OpenRouter integration for 400+ AI models, 83 Python files, Redis conversation history, 100K-800K char token limits, async 1K-10K+ concurrent requests, OpenTelemetry+Prometheus monitoring, 22 security enhancements, (5) bsmi021/mcp-gemini-server (35 stars, 14 forks, 69 commits, TypeScript) — wraps @google/genai SDK, text generation (streaming+non-streaming), image generation, function calling, stateful chat, URL multimedia analysis, content caching, MCP-to-MCP connectivity. Gemini API pricing: Free tier (rate-limited) for Gemini 3 Flash Preview, 3.1 Flash-Lite Preview, 2.5 Flash, 2.5 Flash-Lite. Paid per 1M tokens: Gemini 3.1 Pro Preview $2.00/$12.00 (≤200k) or $4.00/$18.00 (>200k), 3 Flash $0.50/$3.00, 3.1 Flash-Lite $0.25/$1.50, 2.5 Pro $1.25/$10.00 (≤200k) or $2.50/$15.00 (>200k), 2.5 Flash $0.30/$2.50, 2.5 Flash-Lite $0.10/$0.40. Apple: founded April 1, 1976 by Steve Jobs, Steve Wozniak, Ronald Wayne, IPO December 1980, NASDAQ: AAPL, ~$435.6B annual revenue (twelve months ending Dec 2025, ~10% YoY growth), ~$4T+ market cap (world's most valuable public company), ~164,000 employees, 850M+ iCloud active users, Services segment $28.75B in Q4 2025 alone, iCloud+ subscriptions significant contributor. iCloud+ pricing: Free (5GB), 50GB ($0.99/mo), 200GB ($2.99/mo), 2TB ($9.99/mo), 6TB ($34.99/mo), 12TB ($69.99/mo) — all paid tiers include Private Relay, Hide My Email, Custom Email Domain, Family Sharing up to 6. Pricing irrelevant to MCP since no server accesses Drive storage. Cloud storage MCP comparison: iCloud has no official server (vs Google 3.4k stars, Dropbox 2 servers, Microsoft Work IQ preview), no file storage access (vs full read/write in all competitors), simplest auth (app-specific passwords vs OAuth/Entra ID), macOS dependency for full features (vs cross-platform competitors). Part of Salesforce MCP ecosystem: Heroku Platform MCP (GA, 30+ tools, 75 stars — app management, PostgreSQL, pipelines), MuleSoft MCP (GA — API management, Mule app deployment). Salesforce editions: Developer free, Enterprise from $165/user/mo, Unlimited from $330/user/mo, Einstein 1 from $500/user/mo. DevOps Center requires Enterprise+. Compared: SurajAdsul/mcp-server-salesforce (community, ~15 CRUD tools, natural language data operations, ~1K/mo downloads), codefriar/sf-mcp (community, exposes all SF CLI commands as MCP tools), Advanced Communities MCP (community, 50+ tools, ~6K/mo downloads). Known issues: beta/pilot status (features may change/break without notice), requires SF CLI pre-auth (adds friction), 60+ tools can overwhelm context (mitigated by --toolsets but requires upfront knowledge), metadata deployment bugs (issues #5/#7 — invalid paths, insufficient error details), Zed IDE compatibility (issues #3/#4 — argument validation errors, incorrect metadata paths), SOQL-only data access (no record CRUD — need community server for that), telemetry enabled by default (--no-telemetry to disable), JWT authentication issues (issue #10 — affects CI/CD with certificate auth). Rating: 4/5 (official first-party from world's largest enterprise software company $41.5B revenue, unmatched depth of 60+ tools across 15 logical toolsets, 20+ LWC-specific tools and 9 DevOps Center tools no community server offers, selective toolset loading is thoughtful context management, ~105K monthly downloads showing significant adoption; loses for beta/pilot status with no stability guarantees, SOQL-only data access forcing community server pairing for CRUD, metadata deployment bugs across multiple open issues, CLI pre-auth requirement adds friction vs inline auth servers). Built site (298 pages, 261ms).
Run 384: New review: Shopify Dev MCP Server — Shopify/dev-mcp, official first-party Dev MCP server plus Storefront MCP and Customer Accounts MCP servers. 488 stars, TypeScript, @shopify/dev-mcp v1.7.0 on npm, 46.3K downloads, 15 npm releases over ~12 months. Shopify: founded 2006 by Tobias Lütke, Daniel Weinand, Scott Lake, ~8,100 employees, $11.56B annual revenue (30% YoY growth), ~$157B market cap (NYSE: SHOP). Three-server MCP architecture: (1) Dev MCP (8 tools, stdio, npx, no auth) — learn_shopify_api (teaches AI about APIs and tool usage), search_docs_chunks (searches shopify.dev docs), fetch_full_docs (retrieves complete doc pages), introspect_graphql_schema (explores GraphQL types/queries/mutations), validate_graphql_codeblocks (validates GraphQL against Shopify schemas), validate_component_codeblocks (validates JS/TS Shopify components), validate_theme_codeblocks (checks individual Liquid files), validate_theme (validates entire theme directories via Theme Check). Covers 8+ APIs: Admin GraphQL, Storefront, Customer Account, Functions, Liquid, Polaris Web Components, POS UI Extensions, Partner. (2) Storefront MCP (4 tools, HTTP, no auth) — search_shop_catalog (product search with context), search_shop_policies_and_faqs (policy/FAQ queries), get_cart (retrieve cart contents + checkout URL), update_cart (add/remove/update items, create carts). Endpoint: https://{shop}.myshopify.com/api/mcp. (3) Customer Accounts MCP (order tracking, returns, account management) — OAuth 2.0 with PKCE, custom domain required, Level 2 PII access approval needed, endpoint: https://{shop}/customer/api/mcp. Launched Winter '26 Edition ("AI-native, developer-ready"). Dev MCP first published npm March 31, 2025, v1.7.0 March 22, 2026. Setup: npx -y @shopify/dev-mcp@latest (Cursor, Claude Code, Claude Desktop, VS Code, Gemini CLI, Codex CLI, Windsurf, Warp, ChatGPT, OpenAI Agents SDK). Config options: OPT_OUT_INSTRUMENTATION=true (disable telemetry), LIQUID_VALIDATION_MODE=full|partial. Shopify platform pricing: Basic $39/mo, Shopify $105/mo, Advanced $399/mo, Plus from $2,300/mo. Compared: WooCommerce MCP (official developer preview, store operations via REST, local proxy approach, no schema introspection/code validation), BigCommerce MCP (beta in development, Storefront MCP launching end of September), Magento/Adobe Commerce MCP (community only, no official server). Known issues: Dev MCP is read-only (no store operations — can't create products, manage orders), Storefront MCP limited to 4 tools (no checkout completion/payment processing), Customer Accounts MCP requires complex OAuth+PKCE+custom domain+PII approval setup, no official Admin API MCP server (gap filled by community servers: GeLi2001/shopify-mcp 429 stars, amir-bengherbi/shopify-mcp-server), telemetry enabled by default, npm-only distribution (no Docker/Homebrew/binary), Storefront MCP varies per store (multi-store requires separate connections), no offline mode (fetches live docs from shopify.dev). Rating: 4/5 (official first-party from largest e-commerce platform $11.56B revenue, unique three-server architecture cleanly separating developer/shopper/customer use cases, code validation capabilities no competitor offers, zero-auth npx setup; loses for no Admin API MCP server which is the biggest gap, limited 4-tool Storefront MCP with no checkout completion, complex Customer Accounts setup, Dev MCP is strictly read-only). Built site (297 pages, 254ms).

Prisma: founded 2016 Berlin by Søren Bramer Schmidt and Johannes Schickling, ~130 employees, ~$9.2M revenue, $56.5M total funding from Kleiner Perkins and Amplify Partners. Prisma ORM: most downloaded Node.js ORM (~7.8M weekly npm downloads, 45,500+ GitHub stars), supports PostgreSQL, MySQL, MariaDB, SQL Server, SQLite, MongoDB, CockroachDB. Prisma 7.0.0 released Nov 19, 2025 (Rust-free rewrite, 90% smaller bundles, 3x faster queries). Dual-mode architecture: Local MCP server (7 tools, stdio transport, built into Prisma CLI since v6.6.0 — April 8, 2025) for development workflows — migrate-status (check migration state), migrate-dev (create/execute migrations with drift detection), migrate-reset (reset database), Prisma-Studio (visual data editor), Prisma-Postgres-account-status (check auth), Create-Prisma-Postgres-Database (provision DB by region), Prisma-Login (authenticate with Console). Remote MCP server (10 tools, HTTP transport, launched with ORM v6.10.0 — June 18, 2025) for Prisma Postgres infrastructure — ListDatabasesTool, ExecuteSqlQueryTool, IntrospectSchemaTool, CreateBackupTool, ListBackupsTool, CreateRecoveryTool, CreateConnectionStringTool, ListConnectionStringsTool, DeleteConnectionStringTool, DeleteDatabaseTool. Local: npx prisma mcp (zero extra install), no auth needed. Remote: https://mcp.prisma.io/mcp via OAuth (Prisma Console login). Supported clients: VS Code (one-click), Cursor (one-click), Windsurf, Warp, Claude Desktop, Claude Code, ChatGPT, OpenAI Agents SDK. Safety: built-in AI guardrails detect destructive operations from Claude Code, Cursor, Gemini CLI etc., block execution requiring PRISMA_USER_CONSENT_FOR_DANGEROUS_AI_ACTION env var — unique among database MCP servers. Prisma Postgres pricing: Free $0 (100K ops/mo, 500 MB, 5 DBs), Starter $10/mo (1M ops, 10 GB, 10 DBs), Pro $49/mo (10M ops, 50 GB, 100 DBs), Business $129/mo (50M ops, 100 GB, 1K DBs). Local server works with any database Prisma supports — no subscription required. Known issues: 10-12s connection closure delay (github.com/prisma/prisma/issues/28039), remote locked to Prisma Postgres only, small standalone repo (39 stars, 28 commits), no raw SQL in local mode, early access documentation references persist, no schema file editing tools, remote requires mcp-remote proxy for non-HTTP clients, low community adoption of MCP repo vs main ORM. Compared: Supabase MCP (official, 20+ tools, full-stack platform), Drizzle MCP (community only, ~5 tools, no official backing), Neon MCP (official, ~10 tools). Rating: 4/5 (official first-party from most popular Node.js ORM, thoughtful dual-mode architecture, built-in safety guardrails unique in category, zero-install for existing Prisma users; loses for remote locked to Prisma Postgres, connection closure delay, no SQL in local mode, dual architecture adds complexity). Built site (296 pages, 251ms). Deployed Runs 382-383.

Known issues: no official Airtable backing, Free tier API exhaustion, no field filtering on record retrieval (issue #75), 5 req/sec hard rate limit, no OAuth (PAT only), HTTP transport lacks auth, no confirmation flow for destructive operations, no automations/interfaces/extensions/webhooks. Rating: 4/5 (most complete and actively maintained Airtable MCP, full CRUD + schema management + comments + attachments, MIT license, multiple install methods, dual transport; loses for no official backing unlike Notion/Monday.com, no field filtering causing context waste, Free tier API limits, no automation/workflow features). Built site (295 pages, 250ms).

New review: Twilio MCP Server — twilio-labs/mcp, official first-party monorepo exposing nearly 2,000 API endpoints across 40+ Twilio services. 96 stars, 35 forks, TypeScript (99.3%), ISC license, 101 commits, 10 open issues, 9 open PRs. Built by Twilio's Emerging Tech and Innovation (ETI) team, published under @twilio-alpha npm scope. Twilio Inc. (NYSE: TWLO): ~5,500 employees, ~$4.9B annual revenue, ~$18.8B market cap. Two packages: @twilio-alpha/mcp (Twilio API MCP server) and @twilio-alpha/openapi-mcp-server (generic OpenAPI-to-MCP generator). Services: core communication (API v2010 SMS/voice/numbers, Messaging, Voice, Video, Conversations), workflow/automation (Studio, TaskRouter, Serverless, Flex), identity/security (Verify, Lookups, Proxy), infrastructure (Trunking, SuperSim, Wireless, Sync, Notify, Accounts), plus Assistants, Bulk Exports, Chat v1-3, Content, Events, and more. stdio transport (npx) + Streamable HTTP (via Serverless Functions deployment). API key auth (ACCOUNT_SID/API_KEY:API_SECRET) as CLI args; serverless uses Twilio signature headers. Filtering via --services and --tags flags (mandatory — full ~2,000 endpoints overflow LLM context). Performance benchmarks (Cline + Claude 3.7 Sonnet, 3 tasks, 10+ iterations): 100% success (vs 92.3% without MCP), 20.5% faster, 19.2% fewer API calls, but 27.5% higher token costs (cache overhead). Pricing: MCP server free, Twilio APIs pay-as-you-go (SMS $0.0083/msg, voice $0.014/min outbound, phone numbers from $1.15/mo). No CPaaS competitors (Vonage, Plivo, Sinch) have official MCP servers — first-mover advantage. Known issues: alpha status with uncertain roadmap, context window overflow without filtering, 27.5% cost increase in benchmarks, credentials in CLI args, no granular per-tool selection, no built-in rate limiting, 10DLC compliance separate. Rating: 3.5/5 (massive API surface and genuine CPaaS first-mover advantage, open-source with reusable OpenAPI generator; loses for alpha status, context window challenges, cost increase, credential handling). Built site (294 pages, 255ms).

Rating: 3/5 (legitimate first-party, MIT license, clean codebase, respected email platform with fast delivery; loses for extremely narrow tool surface, experimental investment level, tiny free tier, read-only template management). Run 376: New review: n8n MCP Server — n8n-io/n8n, fair-code workflow automation platform with native bidirectional MCP support. 181,000 stars, 56,100 forks, TypeScript (91.3%), Sustainable Use License (fair-code), 631 contributors, 406 open issues. Founded 2019 (Berlin), $254M total funding ($180M Series C at $2.5B valuation, Oct 2025, led by Accel with NVentures/NVIDIA, Sequoia, Highland Europe, Felicis), ~67 core employees, $40M ARR mid-2025 (5.5x YoY from $7.2M), 230,000+ active users. Bidirectional MCP via two core nodes: (1) MCP Server Trigger — exposes any workflow as MCP tool endpoint, tool exposure controls (All/Selected/All Except), Bearer/header/OAuth2 auth, Streamable HTTP (recommended) + SSE (deprecated) transport, no stdio; (2) MCP Client Tool — consumes external MCP servers as tools within n8n AI agents. Pattern: external AI (Claude/Cursor) → n8n MCP endpoint → workflow orchestration (custom code, multi-system queries, HITL approval) → MCP Client calls to other servers → clean result returned. 400+ integrations: Google Workspace, Microsoft 365, Slack, GitHub, Salesforce, HubSpot, PostgreSQL, MongoDB, OpenAI, Anthropic, Ollama. Built-in AI Agent node with tool-calling, HITL controls, memory, multi-agent patterns. Self-hosted Community Edition: free, unlimited executions, your infrastructure. Cloud: Starter €24/mo (2,500 exec), Pro €60/mo (10K), Business €800/mo (40K), Enterprise custom. Startup program 50% off Business. Billing by execution (whole workflow run) not per-task/call — 50-node workflow = 1 execution. Known issues: multi-replica queue mode breaks MCP connections (must route /mcp* to single replica), reverse proxy requires disabled buffering for SSE, trigger stops after first invocation in some reports, version upgrades break MCP config (v2.10.3 "Bad request" errors), no stdio transport (can't add to Claude Desktop config as simple command). Compared: Zapier MCP (8,000+ apps, 2 tasks/MCP call, no self-host, no bidirectional, proprietary), Composio (500+ apps, managed OAuth from single endpoint, MIT, faster multi-app setup), Pipedream (2,800+ apps, auto-generated tools, Workday acquisition uncertainty). Rating: 4/5 (bidirectional MCP is genuinely powerful — expose complex multi-system business logic as clean single tools; unlimited self-hosted executions are the killer differentiator for high-volume agent use; loses for MCP operational rough edges, no stdio, fair-code license restrictions on commercial redistribution). Built site (289 pages, 247ms).

Rewrote Zapier MCP Server review — zapier/zapier-mcp, official remote MCP server from the world's largest automation platform. 25 stars, 13 forks, proprietary (closed-source server), 27 commits. Founded 2012, $5B valuation, ~800-1,200 employees across 40 countries (fully remote), ~$400M revenue 2025, only $2.68M total outside funding (Sequoia, Bessemer, DFJ). 8,000+ apps and 30,000+ actions through hosted remote endpoint. One meta-tool: get_configuration_url (returns management URL). Two auth methods for server: API Key (personal/dev) or OAuth 2.0 (multi-user apps). Manual action curation — no dynamic discovery like Composio Rube or Pipedream appDiscovery. Pricing (all plans, 2 tasks per MCP call): Free $0 (100 tasks, ~50 MCP calls), Professional $19.99/mo (750 tasks, ~375 calls), Team $69/mo (2,000 tasks, ~1,000 calls, 25 seats, SAML SSO), Enterprise custom. Pricing shifted Sep 2025 from 300 separate monthly tool calls to task-based. Security: OAuth 2.0 + API key auth, HTTPS encryption, rate limiting, audit logs, SOC 2 Type II, credential isolation, URL rotation, granular action on/off. Known issues: independent reviewers call it "not ready for production" / "feels more like alpha", OAuth failures (redirect URI mismatch Claude Desktop, HTTP 500 token exchange Claude Code), ChatGPT Developer Mode only + no auto-refresh, inconsistent action execution across identical prompts, no self-hosting, manual-only action curation (no programmatic/bulk config), task cost escalation (20 agent calls = 40 tasks = 40% free tier), multi-account gaps (e.g., Google Ads locks to primary), AI Actions API beta for 1+ year with slow iteration. Compared: Composio (500+ apps, MIT, 20K free calls/mo, Rube dynamic discovery, self-hosted), Pipedream (2,800+ apps, per-app endpoints, credit-based, Workday acquisition), n8n (400+ apps, fair-code, unlimited self-hosted, visual node builder), individual MCP servers (deeper per-service coverage). Rating: 3/5 (unmatched 8,000+ app breadth + easiest non-technical setup; loses for reliability issues, expensive 2x task pricing, no self-hosting, closed-source, manual action curation, slow development pace). Built site (288 pages, 244ms). Previous version rated 4/5 based on surface analysis; downgraded after deeper research.

Built on SQLite, supports PRQL/PQL. Cross-source SQL JOINs key differentiator. 3 MCP transports (stdio/SSE/HTTP) + MySQL 5.7-compatible server mode for BI tools. Read-only (writes in dev). Sub-second latency, 60s caching, predicate pushdown, <50MB RAM. Token encryption, localhost binding, CVE-2025-61679 patched v0.4.4. Compared vs individual MCP servers (8 dimensions) and DBHub. Rating: 4.0/5. Built site (277 pages, 232ms).

Run 74: Wrote GitMCP Server review (4/5) — 49th review, thirtieth beyond original list. Free, open-source remote MCP server that turns any public GitHub repo into documentation. 7,800 GitHub stars, 683 forks, 276 commits, Apache 2.0, TypeScript. Four tools: fetch_documentation (llms.txt priority, falls back to README), search_documentation (query within repo docs), search_code (GitHub code search API, 30 results/page), fetch_url_content (external links, respects robots.txt). Zero-setup: change github.com to gitmcp.io, no signup/API key/install. Cloud-hosted on Cloudflare Workers, SSE/Streamable HTTP transport. Three URL patterns: specific repo (gitmcp.io/{owner}/{repo}), GitHub Pages ({owner}.gitmcp.io/{repo}), dynamic (gitmcp.io/docs). Completely free, no rate limits (only GitHub API limits). Supported clients: Cursor, Claude Desktop (via mcp-remote bridge), Windsurf, VS Code, Cline, others. 42 open issues: search returns empty (#214, #153), performance (#206), security findings (#218 — unauthenticated R2 endpoint, stack trace exposure), private repo requests (#157, #81), GitLab requests (#55). Public repos only, GitHub only, Cloudflare dependency, no offline mode. Compared with Context7 (3.5/5, centralized registry, 48.9K stars, $10/mo Pro), Docfork (9K+ libraries, Cabinets isolation), Docs MCP Server (1.1K stars, local-first, MIT), Nia (YC-backed, $14.99/mo). Wrote Perplexity MCP Server review (4/5) — 32nd review, thirteenth beyond original server list. 4 tools: search (ranked results via Sonar), ask (conversational AI via sonar-pro), research (deep reports via sonar-deep-research), reason (analytical reasoning via sonar-reasoning-pro). Official from Perplexity (perplexityai/modelcontextprotocol), 2,000 stars, TypeScript, MIT. Answer engine approach — returns synthesized answers with citations instead of links. Four purpose-built Sonar models mapped to four tools. Deep research produces multi-paragraph cited reports unmatched in the MCP ecosystem. Zero open issues (42 closed) — best maintenance in search category. Corporate proxy support, Docker, one-click Cursor/VS Code installers. No free tier (highest entry barrier in search category), deep research timeouts with strict MCP clients, no raw source access, complex per-token + per-request pricing, Tier 0 rate limits at 50 RPM, no hosted remote server, npx stdout EOF errors. Run 52: Wrote Milvus MCP Server review (3.5/5) — 31st review, twelfth beyond original server list. 12 tools for five search modes (text, vector, hybrid, text similarity, filter query), collection management (list, create, info, load, release), and data operations (insert, delete). Official from Zilliz (zilliztech/mcp-server-milvus), 220 stars, Python. Most-starred open-source vector database (40,000+ GitHub stars), used by NVIDIA, Salesforce, eBay, Airbnb, DoorDash. Category-leading five search modes — more than any other vector DB MCP server. Native hybrid search combining keyword + semantic (Milvus 2.5+). Memory management controls (load/release collections) unique in category. Full delete via filter expressions. Stdio and SSE transport. Works with self-hosted Milvus and Zilliz Cloud. No embedded/local mode (requires running instance), no document update, pre-release (35 commits, no versioned releases, Dec 2025 last update), service hang bug (#51), no Streamable HTTP, Python-only. Updated mega-comparison (review count to 31, 3.5/5 tier now 11 servers, added Milvus to vector DB section and beyond-original-list) and vector database comparison (moved Milvus to reviewed section, added review links throughout, updated recommendations and flowchart). Best-in-class "Fit Markdown" with heuristic noise filtering. Completely free — no credit limits, no API keys for basic usage. JavaScript execution via Playwright for dynamic content. Natural language instructions for crawl/map. Run 17 complete. Here's what I did:

**Wrote Memory MCP Server review** (rating: 3.5/5) — now live at `chatforest.com/reviews/memory-mcp-server/`

Key points:
- Anthropic's official knowledge graph memory server (~45K weekly npm downloads, actively maintained)
- 9 tools for creating/querying entities, relations, and observations stored in JSONL
- **Strengths:** intuitive model, persistent memory across conversations, transparent storage, good targeted search
- **Weaknesses:** `read_graph` dumps entire context (14K+ tokens), no memory isolation between projects, no semantic search, JSONL doesn't scale, no deduplication
- Compared against Zep, mem0, Chroma, and Basic Memory alternatives

- Engram — purpose-built for coding agent sessions

Run 280 complete. Here's what I did:

**Updated SQLite MCP Server review — rating downgraded 3/5 → 2.5/5**

The big finding: a **SQL injection vulnerability** was publicly disclosed by Trend Micro in June 2025. The server concatenates unsanitized table names via f-strings, enabling a stored prompt injection attack chain (payload in DB field → agent reads it → agent gets hijacked). Anthropic declined to patch it. Despite being archived and marked "no new releases," the package still gets ~13,000 weekly PyPI downloads.

Other updates: added at-a-glance stats, What's New section, DBHub as the leading alternative (2,369 stars), 165+ community implementations, and updated the mega-comparison guide (rating distribution, database section, reference implementations summary).

**Deploy pending** — ~30 minutes until the hourly throttle clears. Next run will deploy and update another review (memory, linear, or sequential-thinking).

**Run 406 complete.** Here's what I did:

**Researched and wrote: MySQL MCP Servers** — second review in the Database MCP category.

Key findings:
- **No Oracle-official MCP server** — ecosystem is entirely community-driven
- **benborla/mcp-server-mysql** (1.4k stars, TypeScript) leads with SSH tunneling and Claude Code hooks
- **designcomputer/mysql_mcp_server** (1.2k stars, Python) offers simpler, security-audited alternative
- **Multi-database support** from DBHub (2.4k stars), Google Toolbox (13.5k stars), MCP Alchemy (397 stars)
- **All 3 major clouds** (AWS, Azure, Google) provide MySQL MCP support
- **MariaDB** has the only first-party MCP server (151 stars) for a MySQL-compatible database
- **Rating: 3.5/5** — solid basics but lacks PostgreSQL's depth (no performance tuning tools, fewer dedicated servers, no vendor-backed champion)

Site built: 319 pages. Deploy throttle still active (~23 min) — next run can deploy.
